# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

## Summary

I've identified and documented all Go source files in prometheus/prometheus that enforce TLS and authentication for remote write endpoints:

**Key Files Found:**
1. **`config/config.go`** - Core configuration structs and validation
2. **`storage/remote/client.go`** - HTTP client creation with TLS/auth enforcement  
3. **`storage/remote/write.go`** - Remote write storage with configuration application
4. **`storage/remote/azuread/azuread.go`** - Azure AD authentication support
5. **`storage/remote/googleiam/googleiam.go`** - Google IAM authentication support

**Key Enforcement Mechanisms:**
- **`validateAuthConfigs()`** - Ensures only ONE auth method is configured (basic_auth, authorization, oauth2, sigv4, azuread, or google_iam)
- **`validateHeaders()`** - Prevents manual authorization header setting, forcing proper auth configuration
- **`RemoteWriteConfig.UnmarshalYAML()`** - Validates TLS config during config parsing
- **`NewWriteClient()`/`NewReadClient()`** - Create HTTP clients with validated TLS and auth settings
- **TLS validation** through HTTPClientConfig.Validate() from prometheus/common/config

The answer includes detailed file paths, relevant symbols, the configuration chain flow, and a comprehensive narrative explaining how Prometheus enforces TLS compliance and authentication for remote write endpoints.

metadata configuration for a remote write endpoint.\n248: \tDefaultMetadataConfig = MetadataConfig{\n249: \t\tSend:              true,\n250: \t\tSendInterval:      model.Duration(1 * time.Minute),\n251: \t\tMaxSamplesPerSend: 2000,\n252: \t}\n253: \n254: \t// DefaultRemoteReadConfig is the default remote read configuration.\n255: \tDefaultRemoteReadConfig = RemoteReadConfig{\n256: \t\tRemoteTimeout:        model.Duration(1 * time.Minute),\n257: \t\tChunkedReadLimit:     DefaultChunkedReadLimit,\n258: \t\tHTTPClientConfig:     config.DefaultHTTPClientConfig,\n259: \t\tFilterExternalLabels: true,\n260: \t}\n261: \n262: \t// DefaultStorageConfig is the default TSDB/Exemplar storage configuration.\n263: \tDefaultStorageConfig = StorageConfig{\n264: \t\tExemplarsConfig: &DefaultExemplarsConfig,\n265: \t}\n266: \n267: \tDefaultExemplarsConfig = ExemplarsConfig{\n268: \t\tMaxExemplars: 100000,\n269: \t}\n270: \n271: \t// DefaultOTLPConfig is the default OTLP configuration.\n272: \tDefaultOTLPConfig = OTLPConfig{\n273: \t\tTranslationStrategy: otlptranslator.UnderscoreEscapingWithSuffixes,\n274: \t\t// For backwards compatibility.\n275: \t\tLabelNameUnderscoreSanitization: true,\n276: \t\t// For backwards compatibility.\n277: \t\tLabelNamePreserveMultipleUnderscores: true,\n278: \t}\n279: )\n280: \n281: // Config is the top-level configuration for Prometheus's config files.\n282: type Config struct {\n283: \tGlobalConfig      GlobalConfig    `yaml:\"global\"`\n284: \tRuntime           RuntimeConfig   `yaml:\"runtime,omitempty\"`\n285: \tAlertingConfig    AlertingConfig  `yaml:\"alerting,omitempty\"`\n286: \tRuleFiles         []string        `yaml:\"rule_files,omitempty\"`\n287: \tScrapeConfigFiles func (c *Config) SetDirectory(dir string) {\n302: \tc.GlobalConfig.SetDirectory(dir)\n303: \tc.AlertingConfig.SetDirectory(dir)\n304: \tc.TracingConfig.SetDirectory(dir)\n305: \tfor i, file := range fmt.Sprintf(\"<error creating config string: %s>\", err)\n326: \t}\n327: \treturn string(b)\n328: }\n329: \n330: // GetScrapeConfigs returns the read-only, validated scrape configurations including\n331: // the ones from the scrape_config_files.\n332: // This method does not write to config, and it's concurrency safe (the pointer receiver is for efficiency).\n333: // This method also assumes the Config was created by Load or LoadFile function, it returns error\n334: // if it was not. We can't re-validate or apply globals here due to races,\n335: // read more https://github.com/prometheus/prometheus/issues/15538.\n336: func (c *Config) GetScrapeConfigs() ([]*ScrapeConfig, error) {\n337: \tif !c.loaded {\n338: \t\t// Programmatic error, we warn before more confusing errors would happen due to lack of the globalization.\n339: \t\treturn nil, errors.New(\"scrape config cannot be fetched, main config was not validated and loaded correctly; should not happen\")\n340: \t}\n341: \n342: \tscfgs := make([]*ScrapeConfig, len(c.ScrapeConfigs))\n343: \tjobNames := map[string]string{}\n344: \tfor i, scfg := range c.ScrapeConfigs {\n345: \t\tjobNames[scfg.JobName] = \"main config file\"\n346: \t\tscfgs[i] = scfg\n347: \t}\n348: \n349: \t// Re-read and validate the dynamic scrape config rules.\n350: \tfor _, pat := range c.ScrapeConfigFiles {\n351: \t\tfs, err := filepath.Glob(pat)\n352: \t\tif err != nil {\n353: \t\t\t// The only error can be a bad pattern.\n354: \t\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"error retrieving scrape config files for %q: %w\", pat, err)\n355: \t\t}\n356: \t\tfor _, filename := range fs {\n357: \t\t\tcfg := ScrapeConfigs{}\n358: \t\t\tcontent, err := os.ReadFile(filename)\n359: \t\t\tif err != nil {\n360: \t\t\t\treturn nil, fileErr(filename, err)\n361: \t\t\t}\n362: \t\t\terr = yaml.UnmarshalStrict(content, &cfg)\n363: \t\t\tif err != nil {\n364: \t\t\t\treturn nil, fileErr(filename, err)\n365: \t\t\t}\n366: \t\t\tfor _, scfg := range cfg.ScrapeConfigs {\n367: \t\t\t\tif err := scfg.Validate(c.GlobalConfig); err != nil {\n368: \t\t\t\t\treturn nil, fileErr(filename, err)\n369: \t\t\t\t}\n370: \n371: \t\t\t\tif f, ok := jobNames[scfg.JobName]; ok {\n372: \t\t\t\t\treturn nil, fileErr(filename, fmt.Errorf(\"found multiple scrape configs with job name %q, first found in %s\", scfg.JobName, f))\n373: \t\t\t\t}\n374: \t\t\t\tjobNames[scfg.JobName] = fmt.Sprintf(\"%q\", filePath(filename))\n375: \n376: \t\t\t\tscfg.SetDirectory(filepath.Dir(filename))\n377: \t\t\t\tscfgs = append(scfgs, scfg)\n378: \t\t\t}\n379: \t\t}\n380: \t}\n381: \treturn scfgs, nil\n382: }\n383: \n384: // UnmarshalYAML implements the yaml.Unmarshaler interface.\n385: // NOTE: This method should not be used outside of this package. Use Load or LoadFile instead.\n386: func (c *Config) UnmarshalYAML(unmarshal func(any) error) error {\n387: \t*c = DefaultConfig\n388: \t// We want to set c to the defaults and then overwrite it with the input.\n389: \t// To make unmarshal fill the plain data struct rather than calling UnmarshalYAML\n390: \t// again, we have to hide it using a type indirection.\n391: \ttype plain Config\n392: \tif err := unmarshal((*plain)(c)); err != nil {\n424: \t\t\treturn err\n425: \t\t}\n426: \t\tif _, ok := jobNames[scfg.JobName]; ok {\n427: \t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"found multiple scrape configs with job name %q\", scfg.JobName)\n428: \t\t}\n429: \t\tjobNames[scfg.JobName] = struct{}{}\n430: \t}\n431: \n432: \tif err := c.AlertingConfig.Validate(c.GlobalConfig.MetricNameValidationScheme); err != nil {\n433: \t\treturn err\n434: \t}\n435: \n436: \trwNames := map[string]struct{}{}\n437: \tfor _, rwcfg := range c.RemoteWriteConfigs {\n438: \t\tif rwcfg == nil {\n439: \t\t\treturn errors.New(\"empty or null remote write config section\")\n440: \t\t}\n441: \t\t// Skip empty names, we fill their name with their config hash in remote write code.\n442: \t\tif _, ok := rwNames[rwcfg.Name]; ok && rrcfg.Name != \"\" {\n457: \t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"found multiple remote read configs with job name %q\", rrcfg.Name)\n458: \t\t}\n459: \t\trrNames[rrcfg.Name] = struct{}{}\n460: \t}\n461: \treturn nil\n462: }\n463: \n464: // GlobalConfig configures values that are used across other configuration\n465: // objects.\n466: type GlobalConfig struct {\n467: \t// How frequently to scrape targets by default.\n468: \tScrapeInterval model.Duration `yaml:\"scrape_interval,omitempty\"`\n469: \t// The default timeout when scraping targets.\n470: \tScrapeTimeout model.Duration `yaml:\"scrape_timeout,omitempty\"`\n471: \t// The protocols to negotiate during a scrape. \n529: // Validate returns error if given scrape protocol is not supported.\n530: func (s ScrapeProtocol) Validate() error {\n531: \tif _, ok := ScrapeProtocolsHeaders[s]; !ok {\n532: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"unknown scrape protocol %v, supported: %v\",\n533: \t\t\ts, func() (ret []string) {\n534: \t\t\t\tfor k := range ScrapeProtocolsHeaders {\n535: \t\t\t\t\tret = append(ret, a particular ScrapeProtocol.\n545: func (s ScrapeProtocol) HeaderMediaType() string {\n546: \tif _, ok := ScrapeProtocolsHeaders[s]; !ok {\n547: \t\treturn \"\"\n548: \t}\n549: \tmediaType, _, err :=
